{"Afghanistan":{"158":{"title":"Poliomyelitis update (23): global (Syria, Pakistan, DR Congo)\r\n\tWPV1, cVDPV2 ","date":["31","Aug","2017"],"url":"promedPRO/EDR> Poliomyelitis update (23): global (Syria, Pakistan, DR Congo)\r\n\tWPV1, cVDPV2 [EXTERNAL]","summary":" A ProMED-mail post (http://www.promedmail.org) ProMED-mail is a program of the International Society for Infectious Diseases (http://www.isid.org)  In this update: <br><br><strong>{1}</strong> Global - Polio Eradication Initiative <br><br><strong>{2}</strong> Syria - WHO Situation Report   <br><br><strong>{1}</strong> Global - Polio Eradication Initiative. Date: Thu 31 Aug 2017. Source: Global Polio Eradication Initiative (edited) (http://polioeradication.org/polio-today/polio-now/this-week/)   Poliovirus weekly update 30-Aug-2017, World Health Organization  New wild poliovirus cases reported this week: 0 Total number of wild poliovirus cases in 2017: 9 Total number of wild poliovirus cases in 2016: 37  New cVDPV cases reported this week: 7 Total number of cVDPV cases in 2017: 47 Total number of cVDPV cases in 2016: 5  Headlines  - Pakistan and Afghanistan polio eradication teams convened last week in Islamabad to follow up on the southern corridor (Quetta Block - Greater Kandahar) joint planning for the upcoming low transmission season. The meeting was attended by the national teams as well as the staff from the southern region of Afghanistan and Balochistan province of Pakistan.  - Summary of newly-reported viruses this week: Pakistan: 2 new wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) environmental positive samples; Syria: 6 new circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) cases; and, DR Congo: 1 new cVDPV2 case. Additionally, pre-notification was received this week of a new WPV1 case from Karachi, Pakistan, the 1st in Karachi since January 2016. The case will be officially reflected in next week's global data reporting.  Afghanistan  - No new wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) cases were reported in the past week. The total number of WPV1 cases for 2017 remains 6. The most recent case in the country had onset of paralysis on 10 Jul 2017, from Zabul province, neighbouring Kandahar province and Pakistan. - Preparations continue for a targeted vaccination round in the southern region of the country, scheduled on 11 Sep 2017  Pakistan  - No new wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) case was reported in the past week; the total number of WPV1 cases for 2017 remains 3. The most recent case in the country had onset of paralysis on 11 Jun 2017, from Killa Abdullah, Balochistan. - Two new wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) environmental positive samples were reported in the past week, from Karachi, Sindh (collected on 7 and 12 Aug 2017). - Additionally, pre-notification was received this week of a new WPV1 case from Karachi, Pakistan. The case will be officially reflected in next week's global data reporting. Karachi had previously been a key reservoir for WPV1 in Pakistan. Analysis is ongoing to determine the origin of this latest case and a response is being planned. The case had onset of paralysis on 11 Aug 2017. The last previous case from Karachi is from January 2016. - The National Task Force for Polio Eradication convened last week, chaired by the Prime Minister of Pakistan and attended by the senior leadership from the national and provincial levels. The Task force reviewed the revised National Emergency Action Plan 2017/18 and discussed mechanisms of accelerating the implementation of strategies to stop WPV1 transmission in the key hot spots. - Under the National Emergency Action Plan for polio eradication, the country is planning to implement 2 nation-wide and 2 sub-national vaccination rounds from September to December 2017.  Nigeria - - No new cases of wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) were reported in the past week. The total number of WPV1 cases for 2016 remains 4 and no cases have been reported in 2017. The most recent case had onset of paralysis on 21 Aug 2016 in Monguno Local Government Area (LGA), Borno. - Nigeria continues to implement emergency response to the detected WPV1 strain and cVDPV2 strains affecting the country (last detected in 2016). - Detection of the polio cases in Nigeria underscores the risk posed by low-level undetected transmission and the urgent need to strengthen subnational surveillance.  Lake Chad Basin  - The detection of wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) (Borno, Nigeria in 2016) and cVDPV2 (Borno and Sokoto provinces in Nigeria in 2016) continue to pose a risk to the neighbouring countries of the Lake Chad basin and hence an outbreak response plan is being implemented as part of the response to the Nigeria outbreak. - Emergency outbreak response efforts continue across the Lake Chad basin, together with activities to fill subnational surveillance gaps across the region.  Central Africa  - One new case of cVDPV2 was reported in the past week in the Democratic Republic of the Congo (DR Congo), from Haut Lomami province, with onset of paralysis on 20 Jun 2017. The total number of cVDPV2 cases this year 2017 is now 8, in 2 separate outbreaks: in Haut Lomami province (6 cases, with onset of paralysis of the most recent case on 20 Jun 2017); and in Maniema province (2 cases with onset of paralysis on 26 Mar 2017 and 18 Apr 2017, with an additional isolate detected in a healthy individual with sample collection on 2 May 2017). - Confirmation of additional cases is not unexpected at this time. Outbreak response is taking place, including use of monovalent oral polio vaccine type 2 (mOPV2) in line with internationally-agreed outbreak response protocols, targeting more than 750 000 children under the age of 5 across the 2 provinces. \n- The 1st mOPV2 round was implemented on 27-29 Jun 2017 in the 2 affected provinces; and the 2nd mOPV2 round ran from 13-15 Jul 2017 in Haut Lomami and 20-22 Jul 2017 in Maniema. - Surveillance and immunization activities are being strengthened in neighbouring countries.  Middle East  - In Syria, 6 new cases of cVDPV2 were officially reported in the past week from Deir-Ez-Zour governorate, bringing the total number of cases in this outbreak to 39. Onset of paralysis of these cases is between 3 Mar 2017 and 10 Jul 2017. The bulk of all cases are from Deir-Ez-Zour, the epicentre of this outbreak. - Confirmation of additional cases is not unexpected at this time and would not change the operational situation, as outbreak response plans are being finalized and implemented, in line with internationally-agreed outbreak response protocols. Two vaccination campaigns are planned for both Deir-Ez-Zour and Raqqa governorates. - The 1st mOPV2 round in Deir-Ez-Zour was successfully carried out between 22-26 Jul 2017. Independent post-campaign monitoring reflected coverage of 88.4 percent (based on caregiver recall). - The 2nd immunization round for Deir-Ez-Zor governorate started on 22 Aug 2017 and is ongoing. Monovalent OPV2 is being provided for children between 0-59 months of age, and inactivated polio vaccine (IPV) for children 2-23 months. In addition to polio vaccines, Aqua Tabs are being provided to families for water purification - 2.5 tons of water purification tablets for 400 000 people have been disseminated at health centers. - Plans are being finalized to mitigate the risks of further spread from the outbreak zone to neighbouring areas and countries, including immunization of at-risk populations in northwest Syria, Turkey and Lebanon.  Officially reported wild poliovirus cases as of 29 Aug 2017  Total global cases in 2017: 9 (compared with 22 for the same period in 2016) - Total in endemic countries in 2017: 9 (compared with 22 for the same period in 2016) - Total in non-endemic countries in 2017: 0 (compared with 0 for the same period in 2016)  - Afghanistan: 6 cases in 2017 (compared with 7 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 10 Jul 2017 - Pakistan: 3 cases in 2017 (compared with 13 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 11 Jun 1017 - Nigeria: 0 case in 2017 (compared with 2 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 21 Aug 2016  Total global cases in 2016: 37 - Total in endemic countries: 37 - Total in non-endemic countries: 0  Officially reported cVDPV cases as of 29 Aug 2017 - Total global cases in 2017: 47 (compared with 3 for the same period in 2016) - Syrian Arab Republic: 39 cases in 2017 (compared with 0 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 10 Jul 2017 - Democratic Republic of the Congo: 8 cases in 2017 (compared with 0 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 20 Jun 2017 - Pakistan: 0 case in 2017 (compared with 0 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 17 Dec 2016 - Nigeria: 0 case in 2017 (compared with 0 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 28 Oct 2016 - Lao People's Democratic Republic: 0 case in 2017 (compared with 3 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 11 Jan 2016  Total global cases in 2016: 5 - Total in endemic countries: 2 - Total in non-endemic countries: 3   <br><br>Communicated by: ProMED-mail. (promed@promedmail.org)   <br><br><strong>{2}</strong> Syria - WHO Situation Report. Date: Wed 30 Aug 2017. Source: WHO UNICEF Situation Report 11 (edited) (http://www.emro.who.int/images/stories/syria/WHO_UNICEF_Situation_Report_11_cVDPV2_outbreak_Syria_29.8.17_3.pdf?ua=1)   Key Highlights  - Six (6) new cases of cVDPV2 were reported this week: 4 cases are from Mayadeen district and 2 are from Boukamal district, Deir Ez-Zor governorate. - The total number of cVDPV2 cases is 39. All confirmed cases to date have had onset of paralysis before 14 Jul 2017. - Final lab results are pending for an additional 5 poliovirus type-2 (PV2) isolates (3 from Mayadeen and 1 from Boukamal districts, Deir Ez-Zor governorate, and 1 from Thawra district, Raqqa governorate). - The 2nd immunization round for Deir Ez-Zor started on 22 Aug 2017 and is ongoing due to high levels of population movement in and out of the governorate during the round. - WHO has organized the redistribution of vaccines and mapping of population movements to increase reach. An additional 90 000 mOPV2 doses are being transported from Damascus to Deir Ez-Zor, to cater for population influxes from As-Sukhnah, Homs governorate, and Al-Qa'im in Iraq. Corrective measures are expected to extend the round by 2 days. - Preparations for the 2nd immunization round for Raqqa are underway. - The total number of AFP cases detected in Deir Ez-Zor governorate since the beginning of 2017 is 122 (91 from Mayadeen, 10 from Deir Ez-Zor, and 21 from Boukamal districts). Raqqa governorate has reported 16 AFP cases (5 from Raqqa, 10 from Tell Abyad, and 1 from Thawra districts). Homs governorate has reported 28 AFP cases (12 from Homs city, 13 from Rastan, 1 from Tadmour and 2 from Talkalakh districts).  more details on the vaccination activities and future plans are available at the source URL as well as the epidemic curve and graphic representation of the vaccination status of non-polio acute flaccid paralysis cases by governorate and district. - Mod.MPP   <br><br>Communicated by: ProMED-mail. (promed@promedmail.org)  In the above global summary, there is still identified transmission ongoing in Pakistan as seen by the positive environmental sample in Karachi as well as the early report on a case of WPV1 associated disease in Karachi. It will be interesting to learn of the genetic profile of the environmental isolates in Karachi (from this past week as well as from a few weeks ago) and compare them with the newly identified WPV1 associated case in Karachi to see if they are genetically related.  There has been more activity associated with cVDPV2 in both Syria and the Democratic Republic of the Congo (DR Congo), with 6 newly confirmed cases in Syria and 1 newly confirmed case in the DR Congo. According to the Situation Report in section <br><br><strong>{2}</strong> above, there are still 5 additional PV2 (poliovirus type 2) isolates in Syria undergoing final testing  4 from Deir al Zour and 1 from Raqqa. Hence there will probably be more cases confirmed in the coming days or weeks. I have not been able to identify similar report information from the DR Congo outbreak so it is not clear if the transmission has been interrupted leaving a total of 8 cases, or if there are still probable cases pending confirmation. The total amount of dead wild boars discovered in the woods around\nZlín, in the far east of the Czech Republic, stood at 94 at the end\nof August 2017. In this month, 23 new infected carcasses were found,\nwhich is a downward trend from July 2017, when 68 reports were sent\nto the World Organization for Animal Health (OIE). The 1st report of\nASF in Czech wild boars was on Wed 21 Jun 2017. Many neighbouring countries have alerted their local pig producers to\nbe very careful what to feed their pigs - and their inhabitants what\nto purchase and how to dispose of it. So did Slovakia, according to\nthe Slovak Spectator. Zlín is only a few km away from the western\nSlovak border, to its north is Poland where ASF has been around since\n2014 and on its eastern border is Ukraine, where ASF has been\nconfirmed since 2011. In a presentation, given in mid-July 2017 to the European\nCommission's Standing Committee On Animals, Plants, Food and Feed\n(SCoPAFF), Dr Petr Šatrán of the Czech State Veterinary\nAdministration indicated that human activities are most likely the\ncause of the spread of the virus, seeing that the nearest reported\ncases of ASF were roughly 500 km 310.68 mi away and that the\npositive dead wild boars were found in inhabited areas. In the other country where ASF was found for the 1st time in 2017,\nRomania, things appear relatively quiet. News broke early this month\nAugust 2017 that ASF was also found on 2 backyard farms in the north\nof the country. Ever since, the Romanian authorities did not report\nany further outbreaks of ASF to the OIE. Of all other countries in the European Union, especially Poland has\ncontinued to report outbreaks of African Swine Fever in smaller and\nmiddle-sized operations. In August alone, on 23 farm sites of various\nsizes, ASF was found to have infected at least one animal, after which\nthe entire herd would have to be culled. The biggest operation in this respect was a farm near Monki, Podlaskie\nprovince, where all remaining 431 pigs had to be culled after 11 had\ndied as a result of ASF, on Sat 19 Aug 2017. Noteworthy as well was\nthe ASF-related closure of 2 farms in Lack, Lubelskie province, in\nearly August. These farms had 136 and 141 pigs respectively see also\nitem 2. Byline: Vincent ter Beek \n<br><br>Communicated by:\nSabine Zentis\nCastleview English Longhorns\nGut Laach\nD-52385 Nideggen\nGermany\n(http://www.cvlonghorns.de)\n(cvlonghorns@aol.com) \n<br><br><strong>{2}</strong> Poland, fence considered.\nDate: Sat 2 Sep 2017.\nSource: Current News summ., edited\n(http://currentlynews.us/articles/poland-will-18857) \nPoland wants to build along the border with Belarus and Ukraine a\nfence preventing migration of wild boars  carriers of the African\nSwine fever ASF. This was said by Poland's Minister of Agriculture,\nKrzysztof Yurgel, Niezalezna reports. As reported, the length of the fence will be 729 km 452.98 mi,\ncosting Poland 130 million zloties (more than 36.2 million USD). The\nfinal decision on a fence will be made within the next 3 weeks. According to experts, ASF has developed in the territory of Poland\n\"thanks to\" the wild boars who entered from Belarus. \n<br><br>Communicated by:\nProMED-mail\n(promed@promedmail.org) The accumulated ASF OIE data from Poland as of Thu 31 Aug 2017, are\nas follows (start of event 22 May 2014):\nNumber of follow-up reports: 189\nTotal outbreaks: 550 (Submitted)\nSpecies/ Susceptible/ Cases/ Deaths/ Killed and disposed of/\nSlaughtered\nWild boar/ - / 620 / 620 / 0 / 0\nDomestic Swine/ 6303/ 402/ 188/ 6097/ 0 A map showing ASF cases reported globally to the OIE since 1 Jan 2017,\nas of Thu 31 Aug 2017, is available at (http://tinyurl.com/ybexasqm).\nClick on the European cluster, zoom in to each of the countries of\ninterest. EU disease control measures require designation of risk areas as Part\nI (wild boar at risk, but no cases found), Part II (wild boar testing\npositive but no spill over into domestic pigs), Part III (cases in\nwild boar and occasional spill over into domestic pigs) and Part IV\nwhich concerns the island of Sardinia only. Consignments of live pigs,\nlive wild boars, meat of either source and animal by-products of\neither source are only allowed under certain derogations. For a full\nexplanation, see European Commission Implementing Decision\n2014/708/EU. ASF, a viral disease against which no vaccine has become available so\nfar, is currently threatening central and western Europe, where dense\npopulations of wild boar are present. According to a recent update of DEFRA (UK) ASF situation assessment,\nthe continuing cases in the Czech Republic, the spread in Poland which\nappears to be due to several breakdowns in biosecurity and the new\noutbreaks in Romania are \"concerning\". This signifies a spread in\ngeographic distribution, a possible drop in biosecurity awareness and\ntherefore an increase in the weight of infection in East Europe. Despite the relatively low level of trade in live pigs, there could be\na substantial movement of people, vehicles and personal imports of\npork products, therefore the risk of ASF introduction to the UK has\nbeen raised from \"very low\" (that is, \"rare but could occur\") to\n\"low\". The Russian veterinary watchdog Rosselkhoznadzor believes ASF will\nkeep moving west via 2 main pathways. The southerly route, has already\nseen the virus spread from Ukraine to Moldova. Russian vets believe it\ncould penetrate central Romania, then move to the Balkans, including\nBulgaria and Serbia. On the northern route, now that ASF has been found in the Czech\nRepublic, Rosselkhoznadzor believes, if it gains a foothold, it is\nlikely to head further west, with Germany next in the firing line. The\nsaid is included in a recent update by the Russian journalist\nVladislav Vorotnikov, available at\n(http://www.pig-world.co.uk/comment/where-next-for-african-swine-fever.html).\n- Mod.AS ","keywordsMatched":[]}},"Belgium":{},"Belize":{},"Bermuda":{},"Benin":{},"Bhutan":{},"Bolivia":{},"Bosnia and Herzegovina":{},"Botswana":{},"Brazil":{},"Brunei":{},"Bulgaria":{},"Burkina Faso":{},"Burundi":{"299":{"title":"Cholera, diarrhea & dysentery update (95): Africa, Asia","date":["31","Aug","2017"],"url":"promedPRO/EDR> Cholera, diarrhea & dysentery update (95): Africa, Asia","summary":"\nCHOLERA, DIARRHEA AND DYSENTERY UPDATE (95): AFRICA, ASIA\n*\nA ProMED-mail post\n(http://www.promedmail.org)\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n(http://www.isid.org) In this update:\nAfrica\n\n<br><br><strong>{1}</strong> Cholera - Kenya (Nairobi)\n<br><br><strong>{2}</strong> Cholera - Kenya (Nairobi) police\n<br><br><strong>{3}</strong> Cholera - Kenya (Tana River county)\n<br><br><strong>{4}</strong>, <br><br><strong>{5}</strong> Cholera - Nigeria (Borno state) IDPs\n<br><br><strong>{6}</strong> Cholera - Sudan\n<br><br><strong>{7}</strong> Cholera, diarrhea - Eastern and Southern Africa Region\nAsia\n\n<br><br><strong>{8}</strong> Cholera - Pakistan (Punjab) \nAfrica\n\n<br><br><strong>{1}</strong> Cholera - Kenya (Nairobi).\nDate: Mon 4 Sep 2017 9:09 AM EAT.\nSource: Capital FM (edited)\n(https://www.capitalfm.co.ke/news/2017/09/cholera-cases-in-nairobi-rise-to-88/) \nThe number of people admitted to various hospitals in Nairobi after\ntesting positive for cholera has now risen to 88. Nairobi Governor\nMike Sonko stated that as at 8 pm Sunday night, 3 Sep 2017, Sinai\nHospital in Rongai had admitted 50 patients who tested positive, while\nNairobi Women's Hospital had 26. Sonko indicated that those admitted\nto Kenyatta National Hospital were 12 and that \"teams from the\nnational and county governments have been on the ground all day.\" He\nsaid that investigations are still ongoing to ascertain and confirm\nthe diagnosis and the sources of the infection. \"The status of all patients is reported to be stable and under\ncontrol.\" He further appealed to city residents not to panic, as\nadequate controls have been put in place to prevent the spread of the\ndisease. \"Above all, let's continue observing high standards of\nhygiene, while ensuring we eat properly cooked food, cleaned\nvegetables and fruits,\" he stated. Byline: Simon Ndonga \n<br><br>Communicated by:\nProMED-mail\n(promed@promedmail.org) Maps of Kenya can be seen at (http://tinyurl.com/kck73tk) and\n(http://healthmap.org/promed/p/174). - Sr.Tech.Ed.MJ \n<br><br><strong>{2}</strong> Cholera - Kenya (Nairobi) police.\nDate: Mon 4 Sep 2017.\nSource: UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs (OCHA),\nReliefWeb, EstAfrican report (edited)\n(http://reliefweb.int/report/kenya/more-90-police-officers-hit-cholera-nairobi) \nAt least 95 police officers have been hospitalized in Kenya with\nsuspected cases of cholera. According to the Health ministry, the\nofficers are said to have been infected after taking meals at the\nNairobi Area Police Canteen. On Sun 3 Sep 2017, some 59 officers were hospitalised in various\nhospitals in Nairobi with another 36 admitted Mon 4 Sep 2017, after\ncontracting the disease. They were part of a group of 430 officers\ndeployed to Nairobi ahead of the Supreme Court ruling on presidential\npoll petition on Fri 1 Sep 2017. They were residing at the\nMultimedia University Hotel in Rongai, about 17 kilometers 10.6 mi\nsouth of the capital. \"Those infected did not get the disease from the Multimedia University\nsince they had their lunch away from the institution. Investigations\nshow that the source is the Nairobi Area Police Canteen,\" said Dr\nRalph Muli, the Nairobi County head of Diseases Surveillance.\nConsequently, the City has temporarily closed the canteen. The Health Cabinet Secretary Cleopa Mailu said the officers were in\nstable condition. Dr Mailu said investigations were underway to\nestablish whether the canteen had outsourced services to cater for the\nlarge number of officers. He said the ministry was concerned that\ninstead of eliminating cholera, new cases were emerging. Nairobi was first hit by the outbreak on 19 May 2017, with 56 cases\nhaving been reported. One of the police officers who requested anonymity said they ate ugali\n(a Kenyan staple made of maize flour) and meat stew at the canteen on\nSat 2 Sep 2017. He said he started feeling sick in the evening. Byline: Lillian Mutavi \n<br><br>Communicated by:\nProMED-mail\n(promed@promedmail.org) \n<br><br><strong>{3}</strong> Cholera - Kenya (Tana River county).\nDate: Mon 4 Sep 2017 10:33 AM.\nSource: KDRTV News, The Daily Nation report (edited)\n(http://www.kdrtv.com/21-people-test-positive-for-cholera-in-tana-river/) \nAt least 20 National Youth Service (NYS) officers have been infected\nwith cholera in Tana River county. County health officials said the 20\nofficers from Bura NYS camp have been admitted to the Bura Sub-County\nHospital. According to Oscar Endekwa, the County Director for Public\nHealth, 21 cholera cases have been reported in the county. Speaking to Nation in his office in Hola, Dr Endekwa said the\nsituation at the NYS camp was under control. \"The officers are\nresponding well to treatment. The other case is of a resident and he\nhas been placed under treatment,\" he said. He added that the symptoms\nwere noted on August 30, though they had not been confirmed, adding\nthat health officials are investigating the cause of the disease. Besides isolating victims, Dr Endekwa said the county is also\nsensitizing residents on hygiene and sanitation. \"We are trying to\ncombat it before it spreads to a larger population,\" he added. He\nasked residents to report any suspicious cases and urged them to drink\nclean water and wash their hands after visiting toilets. \n<br><br>Communicated by:\nProMED-mail\n(promed@promedmail.org) \n<br><br><strong>{4}</strong> Cholera - Nigeria (Borno state) IDPs.\nDate: Mon 4 Sep 2017 2:10 AM WAT.\nSource: Daily Trust (edited)\n(https://www.dailytrust.com.ng/cholera-outbreak-kills-7-idps-in-borno.html) \nOn 3 Sep 2017, 7 internally displaced persons (IDPs) were confirmed\ndead as a result of a cholera outbreak at some IDP camps in Borno\nState This came just 3 weeks after about 100 others were discharged\nfrom Muna and Dala Lawanti Cholera treatment centers. The Médecins\nSans Frontières (MSF) in Maiduguri said the cholera outbreak was due\nto downpours in the last 3 days that caused flood at the affected IDP\ncamps. The Commissioner of Health in the state, Dr Haruna Mshelia said\nmeasures had been taken to contain it from further spread. \"I cannot\ntell you the death toll, as I continue to visit all camps in Maiduguri\nand ensure that the epidemic does not further spread to claim more\nlives,\" he said. One of the rescue workers at Muna Garage IDP camp told newsmen that\nfor only yesterday 3 Sep 2017, they had admitted over 50 patients. \"We have holistic measures to address this cholera outbreak urgently\nalthough people are dying day by day. More than 100 people are\naffected so far, and 51 people were admitted. In the last 24 hours, we\nhave received over 50 patients at MSF's Cholera Treatment Unit at\nDala. Total patients admitted from the start of the outbreak till now\nis over 200 with 100 discharges and 7 dead,\" the rescue worker who\nspoke in confidence, said. The Medical Director of the Médecins Sans Frontières, Anna Cillers,\nalso told newsmen in Maiduguri measures had been put in place to\nprevent further spread of cholera across the metropolis and IDP\ncamps. Byline: Uthman Abubakar, Ibrahim Sawab, Omirin Olatunji \n<br><br>Communicated by:\nProMED-mail from HealthMap Alerts\n(promed@promedmail.org) Maps of Nigeria can be seen at\n(ttp://www.un.org/Depts/Cartographic/map/profile/nigeria.pdf) and\n(http://healthmap.org/promed/p/12103). - Sr.Tech.Ed.MJ \n<br><br><strong>{5}</strong> Cholera - Nigeria (Borno state) IDPs.\nDate: Tue 5 Sep 2017.\nSource: Medical Xpress (edited)\n(https://medicalxpress.com/news/2017-09-death-toll-nigeria-cholera.html) \nThe death toll from a cholera outbreak in restive northeast Nigeria\nhas risen to 21, with most of the victims living in a camp for people\ndisplaced by Boko Haram violence, the health ministry said Tue 5 Sep\n2017. On Sat 2 Sep 2017, the ministry had said the cholera toll was 14 in\nthe town of Maiduguri, with most of the victims living in a camp for\npeople displaced by Boko Haram violence. \"As of 4 Sep 2017, 21 deaths\nhave been reported,\" the Borno state health ministry said, as the toll\nmounts. \"The total number of suspected cholera cases is now 375 in\nMaiduguri,\" it said, up from 186 at the weekend. Most of the suspected\ncases and deaths are in Muna Garage, a camp for displaced people on\nthe outskirts of Maiduguri, while other victims come from neighboring\ndistricts, it said. The government and NGOs are working to contain the outbreak which has\nspread to the town of Dikwa, 60 kilometres (40 miles) away, where 5\ncases had been reported, it added. \n<br><br>Communicated by:\nProMED-mail\n(promed@promedmail.org) \n<br><br><strong>{6}</strong> Cholera - Sudan.\nDate: Mon 4 Sep 2017.\nSource: UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs (OCHA),\nReliefWeb, Radio Dabanga report (edited)\n(http://reliefweb.int/report/sudan/west-darfur-camp-records-six-cholera-deaths) \nWest Darfur\n\nA sheikh in Murnei camp for displaced people told Radio Dabanga that\nby Sun 3 Sep 2017, a total of 22 patients were admitted to the\ncamp's isolation ward. From 27 Aug until 31 Aug 2017, 17 people\nreportedly succumbed to cholera. In Zamzam camp, south of El Fasher\ncity, 4 new cases of cholera were recorded on 1 and 2 Sep 2017. A camp\nelder told this station that the isolation ward was closed on the 1st\nday of Eid Al Adha Sacrifice Feast, 31 Aug-4 Sep 2017, \"because of\nthe absence of medical personnel, so the 4 new patients had to be\ntransferred to El Fasher for treatment.\" Central Darfur\n\nIsolation centers in Zalingei and Abta village, Central Darfur,\nrecorded 3 deaths and 37 new infection cases from 1-3 Sep 2017,\naccording to the coordinator of camps in the state, El Shafee\nAbdallah. In Hamidiya camp, 3 cholera patients died and 13 people\ninfected with cholera reported to the isolation centre. Meanwhile in\nthe last 3 days, the Hassahissa, Khamsa Degaig and Teiba camps\nrecorded 17 new cases. The total number of hospitalized cholera cases\nin the Zalingei Royal Hospital amounted to 76 people as of Sun, 3 Sep\n2017. \"From 1-3 Sep 2017, the isolation center in Abta village near Zalingei\nrecorded 7 new cases. The people are from Abta, Tiri, Dirlo, and\nKalgo,\" El Shafee said. Blue Nile\n\nIn Blue Nile state, 2 people died from cholera and 31 people\ncontracted the disease in the localities Ed Damazin and El Roseires in\nthe last week. A medical source in the area told Radio Dabanga that\nthe Royal Hospital in Ed Damazin received 4 cholera cases of cholera,\nfrom Arquette North. \"2 of them died on Wed 30 Aug 2017.\" Another medical source reported that last week week of 28 Aug 2017,\nthe hospital received 25 cases of cholera from different parts of El\nRoseires. 4 cases were recorded in Gisan locality. \"El Roseires\nlocality recorded the highest number of casualties of all localities\nin Blue Nile. There is a severe neglect of the number of staff in the\nisolation wards, because they were off for the Eid Al Adha holiday.\" Blue Nile was the 1st state to report cases of cholera in September\n2016, or 'acute watery diarrhea' as the Sudanese government has\nreferred to it since the start of the cholera outbreak. A UK-based\nSudanese specialist told Radio Dabanga in January 2017 that cholera\n\"seems to be a stigma for the government.\" \n<br><br>Communicated by:\nProMED-mail\n(promed@promedmail.org) Maps of Sudan can be seen at\n(https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/States_of_Sudan) and\n(http://healthmap.org/promed/p/96). - Sr.Tech.Ed.MJ \n<br><br><strong>{7}</strong> Cholera, diarrhea - Eastern and Southern Africa Region.\nDate: Thu 31 Aug 2017.\nSource: UN Office for the Coordination of Humanitarian Affairs (OCHA),\nReliefWeb, UNICEF report (edited)\n(http://reliefweb.int/report/somalia/bulletin-choleraawd-outbreaks-eastern-and-southern-africa-regional-update-31-august) \nMore than 100 780 cholera/AWD acute watery diarrhea cases and 1496\ndeaths (CFR: 1.5 percent) have been reported in 12 of 21 countries of\nEastern and Southern Africa Region (ESAR) since the beginning of 2017.\nThese countries include: Somalia, Kenya, South Sudan, Tanzania,\nBurundi, Malawi, Zimbabwe, Mozambique, Angola, Uganda, Zambia, and\nRwanda. Somalia accounts for 76.6 percent of the total cases reported\nin the outbreak in 2017, followed by South Sudan at 15.7 percent. In the past 2-3 weeks (weeks 32-34/6-27 Aug 2017), 6 out of the 21\ncountries in ESAR have reported active transmission of cholera/AWD\n(Burundi, Malawi, Somalia, South Sudan, Kenya, and Tanzania). Tanzania\nhas recorded the highest CFR (1.8 percent) followed by South Sudan\n(1.7 percent) in 2017. CFR for Somalia was above 2 percent at the\nbeginning of 2017 but has since dropped to 1.4 percent. Somalia\n-\nThere has been a decrease in the epidemic trend. During week 33 (week\nending 20 Aug 2017), 222 new cases and no deaths were reported in the\ncountry; compared to 282 cases reported in week 32 (week ending 13 Aug\n2017). Out of the 222 new cases, 97 were reported from South Central\nand 125 were from Somali land. Most affected regions are Banadir,\nTogdheer, Awdal, Mjeex, and Lower Jubba. Kenya\n\n4 out of the 47 counties (Garissa, Nairobi, Turkana, and Nakuru) have\nan active cholera outbreak. During week 33, 19 new cases were reported\ncompared to 69 cases in week 32. South Sudan\n\nMost affected populations are nomadic pastoralists and communities\nliving in hard to reach villages and cattle camps. There has been a\ndecrease in the epidemic trend over the past 3 weeks. During week 32,\n30 new cases were reported; compared to 102 cases including 1 death\n(CFR 1 percent) in week 31 (week ending 6 Aug 2017). Active\ntransmission reported in Kapoeta East, South and North, Tonj East,\nYirol East, Nyirol, Ayod, Duk, and Juba. Tanzania\n\nAn increase in epidemic trend. During week 34 (week ending 27 Aug\n2017), 102 new cases have been reported in Tanzanian mainland;\ncompared to 67 cases in week 33. Cases emerged from Mbeya, Iringa, and\nKatavi regions. Malawi\n\nThe current outbreak started within the catchment area of the Chikwawa\nHospital. 11 new cases have been reported in week 34; compared to 2\ncases reported in week 33. Burundi\n-\nThe first case of the current outbreak was identified on 13 Aug 2017\nfrom Democratic Republic of Congo (DRC). Since then there has been an\nincrease in the epidemic trend with 24 cases reported in week 34; as\ncompared to 13 cases reported in week 33. No death has been reported\nand most of the cases emerged from the city center of Nyanza Lac. Uganda\n\nNo confirmed case of cholera in 2017, only AWD cases reported. \n<br><br>Communicated by:\nProMED-mail\n(promed@promedmail.org) The countries mentioned above can be seen located on the map of\nAfrica at (http://healthmap.org/promed/p/6075). - Sr.Tech.Ed.MJ \nAsia\n<br><br><strong>{8}</strong> Cholera - Pakistan (Punjab).\nDate: Tue 5 Sep 2017 12:32 AM IST.\nSource: The Tribune India (edited)\n(http://www.tribuneindia.com/news/this-day-that-year/cholera-in-lahore/462284.html) \nWe understand that cholera is assuming a virulent form in Lahore\nPunjab and that strong and effective measures are called for to\ncombat and stamp out the disease. In Kucha Kharasian in Haveli Mian\nKhan it is said 4 persons were taken ill at about noon and died the\nsame day. The next day, 5 persons were taken ill of the same disease.\nIt is, of course, impossible for laymen to make out whether all these\ncases were of cholera, but the nature of the deaths would seem to\nsuggest the urgent need of effective action. \n<br><br>Communicated by:\nProMED-mail\n(promed@promedmail.org) Maps of Pakistan can be seen at\n(http://www.mapsofworld.com/pakistan/pakistan-political-map.html) and\n(http://healthmap.org/promed/p/2128). - Sr.Tech.Ed.MJ Aggressive interventions to stem outbreaks of cholera include\nproviding sources of clean water and a vaccination campaign. The\nfollowing is extracted from Lutwick LI, Preis J, Choi P: Cholera. In:\nChronic illness and disability: the pediatric gastrointestinal tract.\nGreydanus DE, Atay O, Merrick J (eds). NY: Nova Bioscience, 2017 (in\npress): \"For a variety of logistic, financial, and historical reasons,\nvaccines have not been available for cholera control programs outside\nof Viet Nam. Given as 2 or 3 dose courses, efficacy can be as high as\n60-80 per cent for at least 2-3 years but much shorter protection\nlengths in children younger than 5 years of age. Cost-effectiveness,\nespecially once an outbreak has occurred, had remained unproven until\nreports from Guinea (57) and Haiti (58) demonstrated utility. \"The current vaccines prequalified for use by WHO (59) are:\n- Dukoral (produced in Sweden) that contains several biotypes of O1\nwith recombinant cholera toxin B subunit, which also offers some\nprotection against enterotoxigenic _E. coli_;\n- Shanchol (produced in India) that contains biotypes of both O1 and\nO139 without the recombinant B unit. In a large study in Kolkata,\nIndia, a cluster-randomized, double blind, placebo-controlled study of\nthis product (60), the cumulative efficacy of the vaccine at 5 years\nwas 65 per cent (95 per cent CI 52-74, p less than 0.0001). A\nlocally-produced vaccine similar to this vaccine (mORCVAX) is produced\nin Viet Nam;\n- Euvichol (produced in South Korea) that, like Shanchol, contains\nboth O1 and O139 without recombinant B subunit. This vaccine has been\nreported to be non-inferior to Shanchol in a Philippine study (61). \"In June 2016, the US FDA for the 1st time approved a cholera vaccine\nfor use locally in travelers to cholera-endemic areas. This vaccine,\nVaxchora, is an oral live, attenuated biologic (62) that is a\nreformulation of a previous product. This product, a single dose\nimmunization also referred to as CVD 102-HgR, must be stored in the\nfrozen state and as a live, attenuated bacterial vaccine is not given\nuntil at least 14 days after antibacterials were used and should be\ngiven at least 10 days before oral chloroquine antimalarial\nprophylaxis. Single dose use is an advantage over the older\ninactivated products which are given in 2 doses. Studies, however,\nhave suggested that one dose of these inactivated oral vaccines can be\neffective when the vaccines are in short supply in both endemic and\noutbreak situations (63, 64). \"References\n\n57. Luquero FJ, Grout L, Ciglenecki I, et al. Use of _Vibrio cholerae_\nvaccine in an outbreak in Guinea. N Engl J Med. 2014; 370(22):\n2111-2120; (http://www.nejm.org/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa1312680).\n58. Sévère K, Rouzier V, Anglade SB, et al. Effectiveness of oral\ncholera vaccine in Haiti: 37-month follow-up. Am J Trop Med Hyg. 2016;\n94(5): 1136-1142;\n(http://www.ajtmh.org/content/journals/10.4269/ajtmh.15-0700).\n59. Bhattacharya SK, Sur D, Ali M, et al. 5 year efficacy of a\nbivalent killed whole-cell oral cholera vaccine in Kolkata, India: a\ncluster-randomised, double-blind, placebo-controlled trial. Lancet Inf\nDis. 2013; 13(12): 1050-1056;\n(http://www.thelancet.com/journals/laninf/article/PIIS1473-3099(13)70273-1/fulltext).\n60. WHO. WHO prequalified vaccines.\n(https://extranet.who.int/gavi/PQ_Web/).\n61. Balk YO, Choi SK, Olveda RM, et al. Efficacy of a single dose,\ninactivated oral cholera vaccine in Bangladesh. N Engl J Med. 2016;\n374(18): 1723-32;\n(http://www.nejm.org/doi/full/10.1056/NEJMoa1510330).\n64. Azman AS, Parker LA, Rumunu J, et al. Effectiveness of one dose of\noral cholera vaccine in response to an outbreak: a case-cohort study.\nLancet Global Health 2016; 4(11): e856-e863;\n(http://www.thelancet.com/journals/langlo/article/PIIS2214-109X(16)30211-X/fulltext).\"\n- Mod.LL ","keywordsMatched":[]}},"Cambodia":{},"Cameroon":{},"Canada":{},"Cape Verde":{},"Cayman Islands":{},"Central African Republic":{},"Chad":{"158":{"title":"Poliomyelitis update (23): global (Syria, Pakistan, DR Congo)\r\n\tWPV1, cVDPV2 ","date":["31","Aug","2017"],"url":"promedPRO/EDR> Poliomyelitis update (23): global (Syria, Pakistan, DR Congo)\r\n\tWPV1, cVDPV2 [EXTERNAL]","summary":" A ProMED-mail post (http://www.promedmail.org) ProMED-mail is a program of the International Society for Infectious Diseases (http://www.isid.org)  In this update: <br><br><strong>{1}</strong> Global - Polio Eradication Initiative <br><br><strong>{2}</strong> Syria - WHO Situation Report   <br><br><strong>{1}</strong> Global - Polio Eradication Initiative. Date: Thu 31 Aug 2017. Source: Global Polio Eradication Initiative (edited) (http://polioeradication.org/polio-today/polio-now/this-week/)   Poliovirus weekly update 30-Aug-2017, World Health Organization  New wild poliovirus cases reported this week: 0 Total number of wild poliovirus cases in 2017: 9 Total number of wild poliovirus cases in 2016: 37  New cVDPV cases reported this week: 7 Total number of cVDPV cases in 2017: 47 Total number of cVDPV cases in 2016: 5  Headlines  - Pakistan and Afghanistan polio eradication teams convened last week in Islamabad to follow up on the southern corridor (Quetta Block - Greater Kandahar) joint planning for the upcoming low transmission season. The meeting was attended by the national teams as well as the staff from the southern region of Afghanistan and Balochistan province of Pakistan.  - Summary of newly-reported viruses this week: Pakistan: 2 new wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) environmental positive samples; Syria: 6 new circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) cases; and, DR Congo: 1 new cVDPV2 case. Additionally, pre-notification was received this week of a new WPV1 case from Karachi, Pakistan, the 1st in Karachi since January 2016. The case will be officially reflected in next week's global data reporting.  Afghanistan  - No new wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) cases were reported in the past week. The total number of WPV1 cases for 2017 remains 6. The most recent case in the country had onset of paralysis on 10 Jul 2017, from Zabul province, neighbouring Kandahar province and Pakistan. - Preparations continue for a targeted vaccination round in the southern region of the country, scheduled on 11 Sep 2017  Pakistan  - No new wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) case was reported in the past week; the total number of WPV1 cases for 2017 remains 3. The most recent case in the country had onset of paralysis on 11 Jun 2017, from Killa Abdullah, Balochistan. - Two new wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) environmental positive samples were reported in the past week, from Karachi, Sindh (collected on 7 and 12 Aug 2017). - Additionally, pre-notification was received this week of a new WPV1 case from Karachi, Pakistan. The case will be officially reflected in next week's global data reporting. Karachi had previously been a key reservoir for WPV1 in Pakistan. Analysis is ongoing to determine the origin of this latest case and a response is being planned. The case had onset of paralysis on 11 Aug 2017. The last previous case from Karachi is from January 2016. - The National Task Force for Polio Eradication convened last week, chaired by the Prime Minister of Pakistan and attended by the senior leadership from the national and provincial levels. The Task force reviewed the revised National Emergency Action Plan 2017/18 and discussed mechanisms of accelerating the implementation of strategies to stop WPV1 transmission in the key hot spots. - Under the National Emergency Action Plan for polio eradication, the country is planning to implement 2 nation-wide and 2 sub-national vaccination rounds from September to December 2017.  Nigeria - - No new cases of wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) were reported in the past week. The total number of WPV1 cases for 2016 remains 4 and no cases have been reported in 2017. The most recent case had onset of paralysis on 21 Aug 2016 in Monguno Local Government Area (LGA), Borno. - Nigeria continues to implement emergency response to the detected WPV1 strain and cVDPV2 strains affecting the country (last detected in 2016). - Detection of the polio cases in Nigeria underscores the risk posed by low-level undetected transmission and the urgent need to strengthen subnational surveillance.  Lake Chad Basin  - The detection of wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) (Borno, Nigeria in 2016) and cVDPV2 (Borno and Sokoto provinces in Nigeria in 2016) continue to pose a risk to the neighbouring countries of the Lake Chad basin and hence an outbreak response plan is being implemented as part of the response to the Nigeria outbreak. - Emergency outbreak response efforts continue across the Lake Chad basin, together with activities to fill subnational surveillance gaps across the region.  Central Africa  - One new case of cVDPV2 was reported in the past week in the Democratic Republic of the Congo (DR Congo), from Haut Lomami province, with onset of paralysis on 20 Jun 2017. The total number of cVDPV2 cases this year 2017 is now 8, in 2 separate outbreaks: in Haut Lomami province (6 cases, with onset of paralysis of the most recent case on 20 Jun 2017); and in Maniema province (2 cases with onset of paralysis on 26 Mar 2017 and 18 Apr 2017, with an additional isolate detected in a healthy individual with sample collection on 2 May 2017). - Confirmation of additional cases is not unexpected at this time. Outbreak response is taking place, including use of monovalent oral polio vaccine type 2 (mOPV2) in line with internationally-agreed outbreak response protocols, targeting more than 750 000 children under the age of 5 across the 2 provinces. \n- The 1st mOPV2 round was implemented on 27-29 Jun 2017 in the 2 affected provinces; and the 2nd mOPV2 round ran from 13-15 Jul 2017 in Haut Lomami and 20-22 Jul 2017 in Maniema. - Surveillance and immunization activities are being strengthened in neighbouring countries.  Middle East  - In Syria, 6 new cases of cVDPV2 were officially reported in the past week from Deir-Ez-Zour governorate, bringing the total number of cases in this outbreak to 39. Onset of paralysis of these cases is between 3 Mar 2017 and 10 Jul 2017. The bulk of all cases are from Deir-Ez-Zour, the epicentre of this outbreak. - Confirmation of additional cases is not unexpected at this time and would not change the operational situation, as outbreak response plans are being finalized and implemented, in line with internationally-agreed outbreak response protocols. Two vaccination campaigns are planned for both Deir-Ez-Zour and Raqqa governorates. - The 1st mOPV2 round in Deir-Ez-Zour was successfully carried out between 22-26 Jul 2017. Independent post-campaign monitoring reflected coverage of 88.4 percent (based on caregiver recall). - The 2nd immunization round for Deir-Ez-Zor governorate started on 22 Aug 2017 and is ongoing. Monovalent OPV2 is being provided for children between 0-59 months of age, and inactivated polio vaccine (IPV) for children 2-23 months. In addition to polio vaccines, Aqua Tabs are being provided to families for water purification - 2.5 tons of water purification tablets for 400 000 people have been disseminated at health centers. - Plans are being finalized to mitigate the risks of further spread from the outbreak zone to neighbouring areas and countries, including immunization of at-risk populations in northwest Syria, Turkey and Lebanon.  Officially reported wild poliovirus cases as of 29 Aug 2017  Total global cases in 2017: 9 (compared with 22 for the same period in 2016) - Total in endemic countries in 2017: 9 (compared with 22 for the same period in 2016) - Total in non-endemic countries in 2017: 0 (compared with 0 for the same period in 2016)  - Afghanistan: 6 cases in 2017 (compared with 7 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 10 Jul 2017 - Pakistan: 3 cases in 2017 (compared with 13 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 11 Jun 1017 - Nigeria: 0 case in 2017 (compared with 2 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 21 Aug 2016  Total global cases in 2016: 37 - Total in endemic countries: 37 - Total in non-endemic countries: 0  Officially reported cVDPV cases as of 29 Aug 2017 - Total global cases in 2017: 47 (compared with 3 for the same period in 2016) - Syrian Arab Republic: 39 cases in 2017 (compared with 0 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 10 Jul 2017 - Democratic Republic of the Congo: 8 cases in 2017 (compared with 0 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 20 Jun 2017 - Pakistan: 0 case in 2017 (compared with 0 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 17 Dec 2016 - Nigeria: 0 case in 2017 (compared with 0 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 28 Oct 2016 - Lao People's Democratic Republic: 0 case in 2017 (compared with 3 for the same period in 2016), onset of paralysis of most recent case: 11 Jan 2016  Total global cases in 2016: 5 - Total in endemic countries: 2 - Total in non-endemic countries: 3   <br><br>Communicated by: ProMED-mail. (promed@promedmail.org)   <br><br><strong>{2}</strong> Syria - WHO Situation Report. Date: Wed 30 Aug 2017. Source: WHO UNICEF Situation Report 11 (edited) (http://www.emro.who.int/images/stories/syria/WHO_UNICEF_Situation_Report_11_cVDPV2_outbreak_Syria_29.8.17_3.pdf?ua=1)   Key Highlights  - Six (6) new cases of cVDPV2 were reported this week: 4 cases are from Mayadeen district and 2 are from Boukamal district, Deir Ez-Zor governorate. - The total number of cVDPV2 cases is 39. All confirmed cases to date have had onset of paralysis before 14 Jul 2017. - Final lab results are pending for an additional 5 poliovirus type-2 (PV2) isolates (3 from Mayadeen and 1 from Boukamal districts, Deir Ez-Zor governorate, and 1 from Thawra district, Raqqa governorate). - The 2nd immunization round for Deir Ez-Zor started on 22 Aug 2017 and is ongoing due to high levels of population movement in and out of the governorate during the round. - WHO has organized the redistribution of vaccines and mapping of population movements to increase reach. An additional 90 000 mOPV2 doses are being transported from Damascus to Deir Ez-Zor, to cater for population influxes from As-Sukhnah, Homs governorate, and Al-Qa'im in Iraq. Corrective measures are expected to extend the round by 2 days. - Preparations for the 2nd immunization round for Raqqa are underway. - The total number of AFP cases detected in Deir Ez-Zor governorate since the beginning of 2017 is 122 (91 from Mayadeen, 10 from Deir Ez-Zor, and 21 from Boukamal districts). Raqqa governorate has reported 16 AFP cases (5 from Raqqa, 10 from Tell Abyad, and 1 from Thawra districts). Homs governorate has reported 28 AFP cases (12 from Homs city, 13 from Rastan, 1 from Tadmour and 2 from Talkalakh districts).  more details on the vaccination activities and future plans are available at the source URL as well as the epidemic curve and graphic representation of the vaccination status of non-polio acute flaccid paralysis cases by governorate and district. - Mod.MPP   <br><br>Communicated by: ProMED-mail. (promed@promedmail.org)  In the above global summary, there is still identified transmission ongoing in Pakistan as seen by the positive environmental sample in Karachi as well as the early report on a case of WPV1 associated disease in Karachi. It will be interesting to learn of the genetic profile of the environmental isolates in Karachi (from this past week as well as from a few weeks ago) and compare them with the newly identified WPV1 associated case in Karachi to see if they are genetically related.  There has been more activity associated with cVDPV2 in both Syria and the Democratic Republic of the Congo (DR Congo), with 6 newly confirmed cases in Syria and 1 newly confirmed case in the DR Congo. According to the Situation Report in section <br><br><strong>{2}</strong> above, there are still 5 additional PV2 (poliovirus type 2) isolates in Syria undergoing final testing  4 from Deir al Zour and 1 from Raqqa. Hence there will probably be more cases confirmed in the coming days or weeks. I have not been able to identify similar report information from the DR Congo outbreak so it is not clear if the transmission has been interrupted leaving a total of 8 cases, or if there are still probable cases pending confirmation. Outbreak response is taking place, including use of monovalent oral polio vaccine type 2 (mOPV2) in line with internationally-agreed outbreak response protocols, targeting more than 750 000 children under the age of 5 across the 2 provinces. \n- The 1st mOPV2 round was implemented on 27-29 Jun 2017 in the 2 affected provinces; and the 2nd mOPV2 round ran from 13-15 Jul 2017 in Haut Lomami and 20-22 Jul 2017 in Maniema. - Surveillance and immunization activities are being strengthened in neighbouring countries.  Middle East  - In Syria, 6 new cases of cVDPV2 were officially reported in the past week from Deir-Ez-Zour governorate, bringing the total number of cases in this outbreak to 39. Onset of paralysis of these cases is between 3 Mar 2017 and 10 Jul 2017. The bulk of all cases are from Deir-Ez-Zour, the epicentre of this outbreak. - Confirmation of additional cases is not unexpected at this time and would not change the operational situation, as outbreak response plans are being finalized and implemented, in line with internationally-agreed outbreak response protocols. Two vaccination campaigns are planned for both Deir-Ez-Zour and Raqqa governorates. - The 1st mOPV2 round in Deir-Ez-Zour was successfully carried out between 22-26 Jul 2017. Independent post-campaign monitoring reflected coverage of 88.4 percent (based on caregiver recall). - The 2nd immunization round for Deir-Ez-Zor governorate started on 22 Aug 2017 and is ongoing. Monovalent OPV2 is being provided for children between 0-59 months of age, and inactivated polio vaccine (IPV) for children 2-23 months. In addition to polio vaccines, Aqua Tabs are being provided to families for water purification - 2.5 tons of water purification tablets for 400 000 people have been disseminated at health centers. - Plans are being finalized to mitigate the risks of further spread from the outbreak zone to neighbouring areas and countries, including immunization of at-risk populations in northwest Syria, Turkey and Lebanon. Source: Global Polio Eradication Initiative (edited) (http://polioeradication.org/polio-today/polio-now/this-week/)   Poliovirus weekly update 30-Aug-2017, World Health Organization  New wild poliovirus cases reported this week: 0 Total number of wild poliovirus cases in 2017: 9 Total number of wild poliovirus cases in 2016: 37  New cVDPV cases reported this week: 7 Total number of cVDPV cases in 2017: 47 Total number of cVDPV cases in 2016: 5  Headlines  - Pakistan and Afghanistan polio eradication teams convened last week in Islamabad to follow up on the southern corridor (Quetta Block - Greater Kandahar) joint planning for the upcoming low transmission season. The meeting was attended by the national teams as well as the staff from the southern region of Afghanistan and Balochistan province of Pakistan.  - Summary of newly-reported viruses this week: Pakistan: 2 new wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) environmental positive samples; Syria: 6 new circulating vaccine-derived poliovirus type 2 (cVDPV2) cases; and, DR Congo: 1 new cVDPV2 case. Additionally, pre-notification was received this week of a new WPV1 case from Karachi, Pakistan, the 1st in Karachi since January 2016. The case will be officially reflected in next week's global data reporting.  Afghanistan  - No new wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) cases were reported in the past week. The total number of WPV1 cases for 2017 remains 6. The most recent case in the country had onset of paralysis on 10 Jul 2017, from Zabul province, neighbouring Kandahar province and Pakistan. - Preparations continue for a targeted vaccination round in the southern region of the country, scheduled on 11 Sep 2017  Pakistan  - No new wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) case was reported in the past week; the total number of WPV1 cases for 2017 remains 3. The most recent case in the country had onset of paralysis on 11 Jun 2017, from Killa Abdullah, Balochistan. - Two new wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) environmental positive samples were reported in the past week, from Karachi, Sindh (collected on 7 and 12 Aug 2017). - Additionally, pre-notification was received this week of a new WPV1 case from Karachi, Pakistan. The case will be officially reflected in next week's global data reporting. Karachi had previously been a key reservoir for WPV1 in Pakistan. Analysis is ongoing to determine the origin of this latest case and a response is being planned. The case had onset of paralysis on 11 Aug 2017. The last previous case from Karachi is from January 2016. - The National Task Force for Polio Eradication convened last week, chaired by the Prime Minister of Pakistan and attended by the senior leadership from the national and provincial levels. The Task force reviewed the revised National Emergency Action Plan 2017/18 and discussed mechanisms of accelerating the implementation of strategies to stop WPV1 transmission in the key hot spots. - Under the National Emergency Action Plan for polio eradication, the country is planning to implement 2 nation-wide and 2 sub-national vaccination rounds from September to December 2017.  Nigeria - - No new cases of wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) were reported in the past week. The total number of WPV1 cases for 2016 remains 4 and no cases have been reported in 2017. The most recent case had onset of paralysis on 21 Aug 2016 in Monguno Local Government Area (LGA), Borno. - Nigeria continues to implement emergency response to the detected WPV1 strain and cVDPV2 strains affecting the country (last detected in 2016). - Detection of the polio cases in Nigeria underscores the risk posed by low-level undetected transmission and the urgent need to strengthen subnational surveillance.  Lake Chad Basin  - The detection of wild poliovirus type 1 (WPV1) (Borno, Nigeria in 2016) and cVDPV2 (Borno and Sokoto provinces in Nigeria in 2016) continue to pose a risk to the neighbouring countries of the Lake Chad basin and hence an outbreak response plan is being implemented as part of the response to the Nigeria outbreak. - Emergency outbreak response efforts continue across the Lake Chad basin, together with activities to fill subnational surveillance gaps across the region.  Central Africa  - One new case of cVDPV2 was reported in the past week in the Democratic Republic of the Congo (DR Congo), from Haut Lomami province, with onset of paralysis on 20 Jun 2017. The total number of cVDPV2 cases this year 2017 is now 8, in 2 separate outbreaks: in Haut Lomami province (6 cases, with onset of paralysis of the most recent case on 20 Jun 2017); and in Maniema province (2 cases with onset of paralysis on 26 Mar 2017 and 18 Apr 2017, with an additional isolate detected in a healthy individual with sample collection on 2 May 2017). - Confirmation of additional cases is not unexpected at this time. Outbreak response is taking place, including use of monovalent oral polio vaccine type 2 (mOPV2) in line with internationally-agreed outbreak response protocols, targeting more than 750 000 children under the age of 5 across the 2 provinces. \n- The 1st mOPV2 round was implemented on 27-29 Jun 2017 in the 2 affected provinces; and the 2nd mOPV2 round ran from 13-15 Jul 2017 in Haut Lomami and 20-22 Jul 2017 in Maniema. - Surveillance and immunization activities are being strengthened in neighbouring countries. The total amount of dead wild boars discovered in the woods around\nZlín, in the far east of the Czech Republic, stood at 94 at the end\nof August 2017. In this month, 23 new infected carcasses were found,\nwhich is a downward trend from July 2017, when 68 reports were sent\nto the World Organization for Animal Health (OIE). The 1st report of\nASF in Czech wild boars was on Wed 21 Jun 2017. Many neighbouring countries have alerted their local pig producers to\nbe very careful what to feed their pigs - and their inhabitants what\nto purchase and how to dispose of it. So did Slovakia, according to\nthe Slovak Spectator. Zlín is only a few km away from the western\nSlovak border, to its north is Poland where ASF has been around since\n2014 and on its eastern border is Ukraine, where ASF has been\nconfirmed since 2011. In a presentation, given in mid-July 2017 to the European\nCommission's Standing Committee On Animals, Plants, Food and Feed\n(SCoPAFF), Dr Petr Šatrán of the Czech State Veterinary\nAdministration indicated that human activities are most likely the\ncause of the spread of the virus, seeing that the nearest reported\ncases of ASF were roughly 500 km 310.68 mi away and that the\npositive dead wild boars were found in inhabited areas. In the other country where ASF was found for the 1st time in 2017,\nRomania, things appear relatively quiet. News broke early this month\nAugust 2017 that ASF was also found on 2 backyard farms in the north\nof the country. Ever since, the Romanian authorities did not report\nany further outbreaks of ASF to the OIE. Of all other countries in the European Union, especially Poland has\ncontinued to report outbreaks of African Swine Fever in smaller and\nmiddle-sized operations. In August alone, on 23 farm sites of various\nsizes, ASF was found to have infected at least one animal, after which\nthe entire herd would have to be culled. The biggest operation in this respect was a farm near Monki, Podlaskie\nprovince, where all remaining 431 pigs had to be culled after 11 had\ndied as a result of ASF, on Sat 19 Aug 2017. Noteworthy as well was\nthe ASF-related closure of 2 farms in Lack, Lubelskie province, in\nearly August. These farms had 136 and 141 pigs respectively see also\nitem 2. Byline: Vincent ter Beek \n<br><br>Communicated by:\nSabine Zentis\nCastleview English Longhorns\nGut Laach\nD-52385 Nideggen\nGermany\n(http://www.cvlonghorns.de)\n(cvlonghorns@aol.com) \n<br><br><strong>{2}</strong> Poland, fence considered.\nDate: Sat 2 Sep 2017.\nSource: Current News summ., edited\n(http://currentlynews.us/articles/poland-will-18857) \nPoland wants to build along the border with Belarus and Ukraine a\nfence preventing migration of wild boars  carriers of the African\nSwine fever ASF. This was said by Poland's Minister of Agriculture,\nKrzysztof Yurgel, Niezalezna reports. As reported, the length of the fence will be 729 km 452.98 mi,\ncosting Poland 130 million zloties (more than 36.2 million USD). The\nfinal decision on a fence will be made within the next 3 weeks. According to experts, ASF has developed in the territory of Poland\n\"thanks to\" the wild boars who entered from Belarus. \n<br><br>Communicated by:\nProMED-mail\n(promed@promedmail.org) The accumulated ASF OIE data from Poland as of Thu 31 Aug 2017, are\nas follows (start of event 22 May 2014):\nNumber of follow-up reports: 189\nTotal outbreaks: 550 (Submitted)\nSpecies/ Susceptible/ Cases/ Deaths/ Killed and disposed of/\nSlaughtered\nWild boar/ - / 620 / 620 / 0 / 0\nDomestic Swine/ 6303/ 402/ 188/ 6097/ 0 A map showing ASF cases reported globally to the OIE since 1 Jan 2017,\nas of Thu 31 Aug 2017, is available at (http://tinyurl.com/ybexasqm).\nClick on the European cluster, zoom in to each of the countries of\ninterest. EU disease control measures require designation of risk areas as Part\nI (wild boar at risk, but no cases found), Part II (wild boar testing\npositive but no spill over into domestic pigs), Part III (cases in\nwild boar and occasional spill over into domestic pigs) and Part IV\nwhich concerns the island of Sardinia only. Consignments of live pigs,\nlive wild boars, meat of either source and animal by-products of\neither source are only allowed under certain derogations. For a full\nexplanation, see European Commission Implementing Decision\n2014/708/EU. ASF, a viral disease against which no vaccine has become available so\nfar, is currently threatening central and western Europe, where dense\npopulations of wild boar are present. According to a recent update of DEFRA (UK) ASF situation assessment,\nthe continuing cases in the Czech Republic, the spread in Poland which\nappears to be due to several breakdowns in biosecurity and the new\noutbreaks in Romania are \"concerning\". This signifies a spread in\ngeographic distribution, a possible drop in biosecurity awareness and\ntherefore an increase in the weight of infection in East Europe. Despite the relatively low level of trade in live pigs, there could be\na substantial movement of people, vehicles and personal imports of\npork products, therefore the risk of ASF introduction to the UK has\nbeen raised from \"very low\" (that is, \"rare but could occur\") to\n\"low\". The Russian veterinary watchdog Rosselkhoznadzor believes ASF will\nkeep moving west via 2 main pathways. The southerly route, has already\nseen the virus spread from Ukraine to Moldova. Russian vets believe it\ncould penetrate central Romania, then move to the Balkans, including\nBulgaria and Serbia. On the northern route, now that ASF has been found in the Czech\nRepublic, Rosselkhoznadzor believes, if it gains a foothold, it is\nlikely to head further west, with Germany next in the firing line. The\nsaid is included in a recent update by the Russian journalist\nVladislav Vorotnikov, available at\n(http://www.pig-world.co.uk/comment/where-next-for-african-swine-fever.html).\n- Mod.AS ","keywordsMatched":[]}},"Denmark":{"170":{"title":"Listeriosis - Denmark, Poland: smoked salmon,\r\n\trecall ","date":["31","Aug","2017"],"url":"promedPRO/AH/EDR> Listeriosis - Denmark, Poland: smoked salmon,\r\n\trecall [EXTERNAL]","summary":"\nLISTERIOSIS - DENMARK, POLAND: SMOKED SALMON, RECALL\n\nA ProMED-mail post\n(http://www.promedmail.org)\nProMED-mail is a program of the\nInternational Society for Infectious Diseases\n(http://www.isid.org). Date: Thu 31 Aug 2017.\nSource: HealthMap (edited)\n(http://healthmap.org/ln.php?5286790&u8901) \nDansk Supermarket Group issued a recall after Fødevarestyrelsen\n(Danish Veterinary and Food Administration) detected _Listeria\nmonocytogenes_ in 2 packs of cold-smoked salmon. Byline: Joe Withworth \n<br><br>Communicated by:\nProMED-mail from HealthMap Alerts\n(promed@promedmail.org) The original article, available at the source URL\n((http://www.foodqualitynews.com/Food-Outbreaks/Listeria-outbreak-from-salmon-in-Denmark)),\nis copyrighted and cannot be reproduced. However, it is summarized\nbelow: The Dansk Supermarket Group (DSG) recalled cold-packed smoked salmon,\nmanufactured in Poland, after _Listeria monocytogenes_ was identified\nin the product. The isolate from the product was almost identical by\nwhole genome sequencing to isolates from 3 of 4 patients, whose food\nhistory in 3 of the patients identified the smoked salmon as the\nlikely source. The smoked salmon product was recalled from about 600 stores in\nDenmark and a limited number in Metro Poland. Up to 3 of the 4 patients had become ill in the same week in August\n2017 and the 4th had become ill in May 2017. One of the 4 patients has\ndied. All 4 patients had severe underlying disease. DSG consists of chains (fotex, Bilka, Netto, and Salling) with more\nthan 1400 stores in Denmark, Germany, Poland and Sweden. Refrigerated smoked salmon is a recognized potential source for\nlisteriosis, similar to other cold cut meats and non-heat treated\ncured smoked meats, being a ready-to-eat product that does not require\nfurther cooking before eating. The news report said that more cases\nrelated to this outbreak were expected, despite the recall, as the\nincubation period for listeriosis is up to 3 weeks actually symptoms\ncan start up to as 70 days after exposure. - Mod.ML A HealthMap/ProMED-mail map can be accessed at:\n(http://healthmap.org/promed/p/113). Date: 29 Aug 2017. Source: WSAV (edited) (http://wsav.com/2017/08/29/health-dept-horse-in-bryan-county-tests-positive-for-eee/)   According to the Bryan County Health Department, a horse in Bryan County has tested positive for eastern equine encephalitis (EEE).  EEE virus is a mosquito-borne virus that causes swelling of the brain and is fatal in horses 70 to 90 percent of the time. EEE has also been detected in the mosquito population in western Chatham County, and a horse in Effingham County tested positive for EEE earlier this month August 2017.  The health department encourages horse and large animal owners to vaccinate their animals against the virus and to clean out watering sources, such as buckets and troughs every 3 to 4 days to prevent mosquitoes from breeding in those areas. The total amount of dead wild boars discovered in the woods around\nZlín, in the far east of the Czech Republic, stood at 94 at the end\nof August 2017. In this month, 23 new infected carcasses were found,\nwhich is a downward trend from July 2017, when 68 reports were sent\nto the World Organization for Animal Health (OIE). The 1st report of\nASF in Czech wild boars was on Wed 21 Jun 2017. Many neighbouring countries have alerted their local pig producers to\nbe very careful what to feed their pigs - and their inhabitants what\nto purchase and how to dispose of it. So did Slovakia, according to\nthe Slovak Spectator. Zlín is only a few km away from the western\nSlovak border, to its north is Poland where ASF has been around since\n2014 and on its eastern border is Ukraine, where ASF has been\nconfirmed since 2011. In a presentation, given in mid-July 2017 to the European\nCommission's Standing Committee On Animals, Plants, Food and Feed\n(SCoPAFF), Dr Petr Šatrán of the Czech State Veterinary\nAdministration indicated that human activities are most likely the\ncause of the spread of the virus, seeing that the nearest reported\ncases of ASF were roughly 500 km 310.68 mi away and that the\npositive dead wild boars were found in inhabited areas. In the other country where ASF was found for the 1st time in 2017,\nRomania, things appear relatively quiet. News broke early this month\nAugust 2017 that ASF was also found on 2 backyard farms in the north\nof the country. Ever since, the Romanian authorities did not report\nany further outbreaks of ASF to the OIE. Of all other countries in the European Union, especially Poland has\ncontinued to report outbreaks of African Swine Fever in smaller and\nmiddle-sized operations. In August alone, on 23 farm sites of various\nsizes, ASF was found to have infected at least one animal, after which\nthe entire herd would have to be culled. The biggest operation in this respect was a farm near Monki, Podlaskie\nprovince, where all remaining 431 pigs had to be culled after 11 had\ndied as a result of ASF, on Sat 19 Aug 2017. Noteworthy as well was\nthe ASF-related closure of 2 farms in Lack, Lubelskie province, in\nearly August. These farms had 136 and 141 pigs respectively see also\nitem 2. Byline: Vincent ter Beek \n<br><br>Communicated by:\nSabine Zentis\nCastleview English Longhorns\nGut Laach\nD-52385 Nideggen\nGermany\n(http://www.cvlonghorns.de)\n(cvlonghorns@aol.com) \n<br><br><strong>{2}</strong> Poland, fence considered.\nDate: Sat 2 Sep 2017.\nSource: Current News summ., edited\n(http://currentlynews.us/articles/poland-will-18857) \nPoland wants to build along the border with Belarus and Ukraine a\nfence preventing migration of wild boars  carriers of the African\nSwine fever ASF. EU disease control measures require designation of risk areas as Part\nI (wild boar at risk, but no cases found), Part II (wild boar testing\npositive but no spill over into domestic pigs), Part III (cases in\nwild boar and occasional spill over into domestic pigs) and Part IV\nwhich concerns the island of Sardinia only. ASF, a viral disease against which no vaccine has become available so\nfar, is currently threatening central and western Europe, where dense\npopulations of wild boar are present. According to a recent update of DEFRA (UK) ASF situation assessment,\nthe continuing cases in the Czech Republic, the spread in Poland which\nappears to be due to several breakdowns in biosecurity and the new\noutbreaks in Romania are \"concerning\". This signifies a spread in\ngeographic distribution, a possible drop in biosecurity awareness and\ntherefore an increase in the weight of infection in East Europe. Despite the relatively low level of trade in live pigs, there could be\na substantial movement of people, vehicles and personal imports of\npork products, therefore the risk of ASF introduction to the UK has\nbeen raised from \"very low\" (that is, \"rare but could occur\") to\n\"low\". The\nfollowing is extracted from Lutwick LI, Preis J, Choi P: Cholera. In:\nChronic illness and disability: the pediatric gastrointestinal tract.\nGreydanus DE, Atay O, Merrick J (eds). NY: Nova Bioscience, 2017 (in\npress): \"For a variety of logistic, financial, and historical reasons,\nvaccines have not been available for cholera control programs outside\nof Viet Nam. Given as 2 or 3 dose courses, efficacy can be as high as\n60-80 per cent for at least 2-3 years but much shorter protection\nlengths in children younger than 5 years of age. Cost-effectiveness,\nespecially once an outbreak has occurred, had remained unproven until\nreports from Guinea (57) and Haiti (58) demonstrated utility. \"The current vaccines prequalified for use by WHO (59) are:\n- Dukoral (produced in Sweden) that contains several biotypes of O1\nwith recombinant cholera toxin B subunit, which also offers some\nprotection against enterotoxigenic _E. coli_;\n- Shanchol (produced in India) that contains biotypes of both O1 and\nO139 without the recombinant B unit. In a large study in Kolkata,\nIndia, a cluster-randomized, double blind, placebo-controlled study of\nthis product (60), the cumulative efficacy of the vaccine at 5 years\nwas 65 per cent (95 per cent CI 52-74, p less than 0.0001). A\nlocally-produced vaccine similar to this vaccine (mORCVAX) is produced\nin Viet Nam;\n- Euvichol (produced in South Korea) that, like Shanchol, contains\nboth O1 and O139 without recombinant B subunit. This vaccine has been\nreported to be non-inferior to Shanchol in a Philippine study (61). \"In June 2016, the US FDA for the 1st time approved a cholera vaccine\nfor use locally in travelers to cholera-endemic areas. This vaccine,\nVaxchora, is an oral live, attenuated biologic (62) that is a\nreformulation of a previous product. This product, a single dose\nimmunization also referred to as CVD 102-HgR, must be stored in the\nfrozen state and as a live, attenuated bacterial vaccine is not given\nuntil at least 14 days after antibacterials were used and should be\ngiven at least 10 days before oral chloroquine antimalarial\nprophylaxis. Single dose use is an advantage over the older\ninactivated products which are given in 2 doses. Studies, however,\nhave suggested that one dose of these inactivated oral vaccines can be\neffective when the vaccines are in short supply in both endemic and\noutbreak situations (63, 64). \"References\n\n57. According to the Health ministry, the\nofficers are said to have been infected after taking meals at the\nNairobi Area Police Canteen. On Sun 3 Sep 2017, some 59 officers were hospitalised in various\nhospitals in Nairobi with another 36 admitted Mon 4 Sep 2017, after\ncontracting the disease. They were part of a group of 430 officers\ndeployed to Nairobi ahead of the Supreme Court ruling on presidential\npoll petition on Fri 1 Sep 2017. They were residing at the\nMultimedia University Hotel in Rongai, about 17 kilometers 10.6 mi\nsouth of the capital. \"Those infected did not get the disease from the Multimedia University\nsince they had their lunch away from the institution. Investigations\nshow that the source is the Nairobi Area Police Canteen,\" said Dr\nRalph Muli, the Nairobi County head of Diseases Surveillance.\nConsequently, the City has temporarily closed the canteen. He said the ministry was concerned that\ninstead of eliminating cholera, new cases were emerging. Nairobi was first hit by the outbreak on 19 May 2017, with 56 cases\nhaving been reported. One of the police officers who requested anonymity said they ate ugali\n(a Kenyan staple made of maize flour) and meat stew at the canteen on\nSat 2 Sep 2017. He said he started feeling sick in the evening. The\nfollowing is extracted from Lutwick LI, Preis J, Choi P: Cholera. In:\nChronic illness and disability: the pediatric gastrointestinal tract.\nGreydanus DE, Atay O, Merrick J (eds). NY: Nova Bioscience, 2017 (in\npress): \"For a variety of logistic, financial, and historical reasons,\nvaccines have not been available for cholera control programs outside\nof Viet Nam. Given as 2 or 3 dose courses, efficacy can be as high as\n60-80 per cent for at least 2-3 years but much shorter protection\nlengths in children younger than 5 years of age. Cost-effectiveness,\nespecially once an outbreak has occurred, had remained unproven until\nreports from Guinea (57) and Haiti (58) demonstrated utility. \"The current vaccines prequalified for use by WHO (59) are:\n- Dukoral (produced in Sweden) that contains several biotypes of O1\nwith recombinant cholera toxin B subunit, which also offers some\nprotection against enterotoxigenic _E. coli_;\n- Shanchol (produced in India) that contains biotypes of both O1 and\nO139 without the recombinant B unit. In a large study in Kolkata,\nIndia, a cluster-randomized, double blind, placebo-controlled study of\nthis product (60), the cumulative efficacy of the vaccine at 5 years\nwas 65 per cent (95 per cent CI 52-74, p less than 0.0001). A\nlocally-produced vaccine similar to this vaccine (mORCVAX) is produced\nin Viet Nam;\n- Euvichol (produced in South Korea) that, like Shanchol, contains\nboth O1 and O139 without recombinant B subunit. This vaccine has been\nreported to be non-inferior to Shanchol in a Philippine study (61). \"In June 2016, the US FDA for the 1st time approved a cholera vaccine\nfor use locally in travelers to cholera-endemic areas. This vaccine,\nVaxchora, is an oral live, attenuated biologic (62) that is a\nreformulation of a previous product. This product, a single dose\nimmunization also referred to as CVD 102-HgR, must be stored in the\nfrozen state and as a live, attenuated bacterial vaccine is not given\nuntil at least 14 days after antibacterials were used and should be\ngiven at least 10 days before oral chloroquine antimalarial\nprophylaxis. Single dose use is an advantage over the older\ninactivated products which are given in 2 doses. Studies, however,\nhave suggested that one dose of these inactivated oral vaccines can be\neffective when the vaccines are in short supply in both endemic and\noutbreak situations (63, 64). \"References\n\n57. Effectiveness of oral\ncholera vaccine in Haiti: 37-month follow-up. Am J Trop Med Hyg. 2016;\n94(5): 1136-1142;\n(http://www.ajtmh.org/content/journals/10.4269/ajtmh.15-0700).\n59.
